Family of Han Donghui Demands

Suppression of Gold Exchange 157

Appeals to City Party Headquarters and Social Affairs Bureau Yesterday

To Preserve Public Tranquility and Uphold Humanitarianism

According to the Xin Xin News Agency, Han Donghui from Yuyao, Zhejiang, was suddenly knocked down and died of suffocation by a colleague at the Gold Exchange while negotiating a transaction. His family claims that Han's death was due to the exchange's inadequate facilities and chaotic market conditions. Furthermore, the responsible authorities failed to maintain order, leading to this unfortunate incident. It is also reported that the deceased's wife, Mrs. Han Hong, appealed to the City Party Headquarters and the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday, requesting a severe crackdown to maintain public tranquility and console the departed soul. The original petition is recorded below: A petition regarding the Gold Exchange's negligence of duties, disruption of order, tragic loss of life, and concealment of the perpetrator, requesting a thorough investigation and improvement to uphold humanitarianism and ensure public tranquility. My husband, Han Donghui, used to frequent the Gold Exchange to negotiate margin trading. On the morning of August 22nd this year, after breakfast, he went to the Gold Exchange market as usual to inquire about market fluctuations. Shortly after leaving home, the news came that my husband had been knocked to the ground in the market, unconscious. He was taken to Renji Hospital by car. Upon hearing the news, I rushed to Renji Hospital, only to find that my husband had already died and his body had been placed in the morgue. In just two hours, he had passed away forever, leaving behind no last words or clear cause of death. As a bereaved woman with no education, I was overwhelmed with fear and at a loss for what to do. Fortunately, with the support of relatives and friends, I managed to arrange the funeral. As my mind began to clear, I felt that my husband was in the prime of his life and could not have died suddenly from a mere collision. I suspected foul play or some other cause. With a body pregnant with his child, I braved the autumn chill, wandering around, hoping to uncover the perpetrator's name and clear his name. Unexpectedly, the Gold Exchange treated this tragedy in their market as a common occurrence. They did not detain the perpetrator at the scene, nor did they report the perpetrator's name afterward. They allowed my husband to die and his child to be orphaned, leaving me, a widow carrying his unborn child, to suffer under economic hardship, with no recourse. Any person with compassion would be saddened by this situation, but it is futile to discuss this with the directors of the Gold Exchange. Later, newspaper reports only mentioned that the person who knocked down my husband was an employee of a certain gold firm, without providing their name or identity. This is all due to the exchange's attempts to cover up the truth, allowing the perpetrator to remain at large. The reason for this concealment is undoubtedly related to the chaotic order and inadequate facilities of the exchange, as reported in the newspapers. The exchange is a place where crowds gather, and its market should be spacious. However, the Gold Exchange's market is an old-fashioned warehouse with a small area and a long, narrow shape. Compared to the yarn and cloth exchange, the securities exchange, and the goods exchange in the same area, its

Equipment Inferiority 158

is as different as heaven and earth. Furthermore, the Gold Exchange has the highest volume of trading and the most intense activity. Every day, from the opening to the closing bell, trading is constant. Unlike the yarn and cloth and securities exchanges, which have separate sessions, those who stand there cannot disperse as they do in other exchanges. The number of brokers, over 130, is the highest among all exchanges. Each broker also has several agents who constantly stand in the market. In a small space, an excessive number of people are crowded together, making it impossible to ensure air circulation and unobstructed passage. My husband was knocked to the ground, and if it were not for the suffocating air, he would not have died of suffocation. My husband's death cannot be attributed to the exchange's failure to pay attention to its facilities. Furthermore, the exchange is a place where public prices are determined, and its order should be strictly maintained. However, because the Gold Exchange's market is too small, it lacks a trading center, making management difficult. Furthermore, the exchange's directors only care about their own interests and disregard public safety, leading to bizarre and uncontrollable situations in the market. Reports indicate that the market is crowded and disorderly during trading hours, to the point of being impenetrable. In the market, there are even those who resort to violence to compete. In this chaotic state, the concept of abiding by the law has long been swept away by the tide of evil.

Seeds of Murderous Intent 159

are sown by adverse circumstances. My husband's death cannot be attributed to the Gold Exchange's failure to pay attention to management. The Gold Exchange, aware of its own weaknesses as described above, fears that the perpetrator will be caught, lawsuits will arise, and public opinion will focus on its negligence in management and facilities. Therefore, the directors responsible for operations turn a deaf ear and blind eye, hoping to make the death case disappear without a trace. The employee of a certain gold firm who harmed my husband, with this tacit protection, can hide in the gold market and enjoy killing. But my whole family suffers. Upon investigation, my husband was killed in the Gold Exchange market, and the perpetrator was an employee of a certain gold firm. The exchange's directors are responsible for managing the entire exchange, and their authority makes investigating the matter as easy as turning their hands. Furthermore, the exchange's directors and the various gold firms are in the same industry, so there is no reason why they cannot find out the name of the employee of a certain gold firm. They only

Fear Casting Pearls Before Swine 160

and dare not publicly report the matter, thus tacitly protecting the perpetrator. I beseech your department, as leaders of the people, to love the people as if they were infants. Under the clear blue sky, there is such a situation. With the thought of alleviating hunger and thirst, please seek the benefit of the entire society. Now, there is a Gold Exchange director who relies on economic power to protect a murderer. I must ask you to investigate rigorously. Furthermore, the exchange's inadequate facilities and negligent management pose a great threat to public safety. I must ask you to take severe measures to suppress it. Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai City Party Headquarters and Social Affairs Bureau, Petitioner: Han Hong

Assassin of Shao Wenbin Arrested 161

Assassin Zhang Bingrong Confesses to Killing Shao

Claims He Was Instigated by Wang Shilong

Shao Wenbin, formerly a professional storyteller known as "Ma Fu A Liu," resided at No. 19 Zhilan Fang, Kaizi'er Road, French Concession. At the age of fifty, he abandoned his old profession and switched to operating flower gambling businesses, creating deep grudges with others in the same line of work. In addition, the authorities were strictly arresting flower gambling leaders, so Shao dared not stay at home and opened a hostel as a temporary residence. On the afternoon of July 28th this year, Shao finished bathing at Xiaoyao Pool and visited a friend at the Far East Hotel on Xizang Road. At 8:00 PM, he left the Far East Hotel, intending to return home for dinner. Unexpectedly, someone was waiting to assassinate him on Huagene Road in the French Concession. When the assassins saw Shao approaching, they suddenly rushed forward and opened fire. Shao hurriedly tried to escape but slipped and fell. He was hit by five bullets and died instantly. Seeing that their goal was achieved, the assassins scattered and fled. One assassin fled north from Hongyun Fang, into the public concession area of ​​Edward Road. He was pursued by someone behind him, so the Chinese and Indian patrol officers of the Xinzha Police Station, who heard the sound, helped to apprehend him. The assassin resisted arrest by shooting. The patrol officers also drew their guns and fired back, causing the assassin to be shot fourteen times and fall at the intersection of Longmen Road. At that time, both sides exchanged gunfire, and stray bullets injured Fan Zhongyi, Hu Ju, Shen Zhaorong, and the elderly woman Tan Zhou, who were sitting and cooling off, in their legs. The Xinzha Police Station sent patrol officers to send the assassin and those injured by stray bullets to Renji Hospital. The assassin died in the hospital due to his serious injuries. Afterward, the French police sent detectives to take Shao's body and the assassin's body to the morgue. The next day, the Second Special District Court sent personnel to examine the bodies. Shao's family collected the body for burial, and the assassin's body was buried by the Tongren Fuyuan Hall because no family members claimed it. The details have already been recorded in previous reports. After this case occurred, the French police were very strict in arresting the criminals. The Chinese and Western detectives of the Xinzha Police Station in the former New Public Concession arrested Yongren Zhang Bingrong (21 years old) in No. 68 Hongfu Lane on Xinzha Road while searching for bandits. It was found that he was one of the main culprits in the Shao Wenbin assassination case. The French police were immediately notified. Jin Jiulin, the Inspector General of the Special Agency, sent detective Zhang Ziying, Qian Yumin, and detective Zhang Chunsheng, and others to rush to the Xinzha Police Station and take Zhang back to the police station overnight. It was found that Zhang's original name was Zhang Bingyun. In the spring of the 18th year of the Republic of China, he was detained by the Public Police Station and sent to the First Special District Court for trial for the crime of privately possessing firearms and theft. After the trial, he was sentenced to four years and two months of imprisonment and ten years of deprivation of civil rights on February 25th. He was released last year on November 27th during the general amnesty while serving his sentence in prison. When questioned about the Shao murder case, he admitted it without hesitation. He was immediately taken into custody. Yesterday afternoon, he was sent to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court for trial by Judge Xiong Huicai. Gu Shouxi, the lawyer of the police station, stated the case, saying that the defendant was involved in the assassination of Shao Wenbin on the evening of July 28th and was arrested by the Xinzha Police Station yesterday. The French police transferred him to the case. Because the police station still needs to conduct a detailed investigation to arrest the instigator and accomplices, he requested a postponement of two weeks and temporarily detain the defendant until the investigation is clear before filing a lawsuit. When Zhang Bingrong was questioned, he confessed that he was a painter in the past, but now he has nothing to do and no place to live. He admitted that the murder of Shao was instigated by Wang Shilong, who gathered Chen Changgen, who is still at large, and Shi Sigen, who was killed, and me to assassinate Shao. Shao and Wang are all members of the flower association. Because of their feud, Wang gathered us and promised to give us a salary to eat after the event was completed. The court verified the confession and ordered a postponement of the trial to the 29th for further investigation. The defendant was still detained.

Municipal Public Security Bureau Cracks Down on Counterfeit Money Selling Organization 162

Detains Four Male and Female Criminals

Confiscates Chinese Counterfeit Money

Ren Yushan, a 33-year-old from Hebei, has no permanent occupation. He came to Shanghai from his hometown and rented a residence at No. 235 South Nanlin Lane, Xinjiang Road, Zhabei, specializing in selling counterfeit banknotes of the two Chinese banks. Ren established a wholesale organization at home. In addition to employing several salesmen (commonly known as brokers) in this city to go to various yanzike and teahouses and restaurants to negotiate prices, he also transported them to various places outside the city for sale. The price of each hundred yuan of counterfeit money was forty yuan, and the sales were very wide. Ren reaped huge profits, but the matter was not kept secret. Inspector Mei Maosheng of the Municipal Public Security Bureau discovered it and reported the previous information to the Inspector General. He was approved by Director Wen to order three plainclothes policemen from the first squadron of the police bureau to go to a teahouse within the territory of a certain tea shop in the fourth district of Zhabei with Inspector Mei at about 10 o'clock in the morning. After the informant pointed out the target, Mei took out twenty yuan and pretended to be a seller to negotiate prices with the broker and purchased five counterfeit ten yuan banknotes of the Bank of China for a total of fifty yuan and learned that the selling organization was located at a certain place. Subsequently, the officials and others took the informant back to No. 235 Nanlin Lane, Xinjiang Road, and arrested on the spot the main criminal from Hebei, Ren Yushan, who was selling counterfeit banknotes, and seized a counterfeit ten yuan banknote of the Bank of China and sixteen counterfeit five yuan banknotes of the Bank of Communications. He was taken back to the bureau for strict interrogation. According to Ren's confession, he admitted to selling counterfeit banknotes and confessed that he had an accomplice, Cao Bingsen from Zhenjiang (47 years old), who was hiding at No. 11 Daji Road, Xiaoximen, Nanshi. Ren was escorted to the crime scene, accompanied by policemen from the second district, and arrested Cao at about 1 pm. According to Cao's confession, the secret contact point for the counterfeit money organization was set up at No. 30 Aifu Lane, Taiping Bridge, French Concession. The counterfeit money was mostly sold by the main organ. The original case handlers escorted Cao to the French Concession police station, together with Lu Ying, the captain of the Criminal Investigation Team, and dispatched detectives Zhao Wenzhong and others. They also dispatched the 12th West Detective and the 108th Chinese Detective to go to the address at 2 pm. Unexpectedly, the bandits had already fled upon hearing the news and disappeared without a trace. After searching, nothing was found, and only the second landlord, Lu Huang, a woman from Danyang (43 years old), and Xu Bingji, a suspect from Anhui, were taken to the bureau for interrogation. In total, four male and female bandits were arrested in the case, along with the counterfeit money, and were sent to the Third Section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau yesterday morning to be dealt with according to law. It is reported that the bureau will notify the two Chinese banks to investigate.

Two Men Bombard a Youth 176

The two men claimed to be military police; the youth was said to be a political prisoner

Yesterday at approximately 2:30 PM, at the intersection of Rue Corneille and Avenue Haig in western Shanghai, in front of the Dajia Kuifeng Department Store, a youth of about twenty years of age was walking along. Fortunately, the nearby patrol officer and Song Ziming, the police chief of the Sixth District Singapore Road Police Station, heard the shots and rushed to the scene. The injured youth (who identified himself as Li Ning) was first sent by car to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment. The bullet had not yet exited, and his life may be out of danger. After questioning by the district chief, the two men, one identified as Qiao Chuntao and the other as Li Rong, both claimed to be sergeants in the First Battalion of the Military Police Headquarters. However, the two men were wearing plainclothes and had no insignia, which seemed suspicious. A decision was made to prepare a written report and transfer them to the General Bureau for further questioning.

Postal Workers' Union Held Emergency Executive and Supervisory Meeting 178

Expressing concern over the serious postal strike in Hankou

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union, regarding the postal authorities' denial of the Hankou Postal Workers' Union as a major serious incident in the history of the postal workers' union, convened an emergency joint meeting of all executive and supervisory committee members yesterday afternoon to discuss active assistance measures. All executive and supervisory committee members attended. After Chairman Fan Caicong reported the purpose of the meeting, Zhu Xuefan, a standing committee member of the National Postal Workers' General Union, attended and reported on the detailed process of the Hankou postal strike. The following measures were unanimously decided on the spot: (1) Send a telegram to Hankou promising to provide assistance with strength, (2) Expand publicity, (3) Issue a statement to all sectors of society, (4) Set a deadline for a final warning to the authorities, (5) Post slogans throughout the various postal service bureaus, (6) Secretly. The union issued the following statement to all sectors of society: Public Notice to All Sectors of Society Nationwide, The organization of our postal workers' union, although it originated in Shanghai, was subsequently established in Tianjin, Beiping, Nanjing, Jinan, Kaifeng, Changsha, and other major commercial ports. The initial purpose of its organization was to support the revolution and serve the country as its greatest goal. For the past ten years, our postal workers' unions in various regions have been committed to consistent efforts. Whether towards the country or towards society, although we dare not boast of our achievements, the facts speak for themselves and have been recognized by all sectors of society. Furthermore, our postal workers' union has never failed the country or society. Moreover, now that the country is facing numerous difficulties, our postal workers nationwide are upholding their patriotic zeal in the hope of being able to serve the people. Unexpectedly, at this time, an incident occurred in which the postal authorities denied the Hankou Postal Workers' Union. The Hankou Postal Workers' Union, at the beginning of its establishment, received instructions from the Hankou Special City Party Department. In addition to being approved for filing, it was also forwarded to the Central Party Department for filing. Thus, the Hankou Postal Workers' Union already has a legal basis for its establishment, which is no different from that relied upon by the postal workers' unions in other regions as legitimate organizations. However, the postal authorities actually refused to recognize the Hankou Postal Workers' Union, calling it an illegal organization. Since this incident occurred, our union has regarded it as a major serious event in the history of the postal workers' union. The postal workers' unions that have been established in various regions, numbering no fewer than sixty, have all been formally recognized by the postal authorities, and some have even been given financial assistance. Why is it that this time the Hankou Postal Workers' Union is being uniquely denied, being called illegitimate? The postal workers' unions throughout the country are all the same, so what is the point of the postal authorities' subsidies and recognition? Our union has pondered this repeatedly, and upon further investigation, we have suddenly realized that the postal authorities have other sinister motives. Their sole aim is to destroy the organization of our entire postal workers' union. Therefore, they are first launching an attack in Hankou, which is also a continuation of actions carried out throughout the country. Nothing could be more serious than this. I still remember when the postal protection movement occurred in the past, those treacherous villains hired a group of lackeys in an attempt to seize our postal workers' union, but they failed. Now they are changing their strategy and attacking from another direction in order to achieve their ultimate goal. Thinking of this, I cannot help but feel outraged. Therefore, I am exposing their conspiracy to inform all sectors of society. As for our union, on the one hand, we see the postal service in danger, and on the other hand, we are personally affected by the situation. Where there is justice, we dare not fail to fight. We hope that all sectors of society will understand and instruct us. We would be most grateful.

Prelude to the Opening of the Family Industrial Cooperative on September 18th 180

Before the "Invincible" Tooth Powder was launched, the national market was dominated by Japanese goods. Customs investigations showed that imports were over 4 million yuan per year. Tianxu Wosheng, a well-known figure in the press, aspired to the great cause of industry. Together with his son, Mr. Chen Xiaodie, he founded the Family Industrial Cooperative to manufacture "Invincible" Tooth Powder. The initial capital was only 10,000 yuan. The total capital has reached nearly one million yuan, and the number of workers is in the thousands. However, there is no large-scale distribution center. All those who love "Invincible" domestic products have been looking forward to it. Now, the cooperative is using the spirit of "Invincible" to organize a new scientific management method, dividing the factory and distribution center into two major divisions. The factory is headed by Director Li Xinfu, and the sales are headed by Director Chen Xiaodie. The "Invincible" distribution center is located at the mouth of the ball field on Nanjing Road. All the decorations are designed by Chen Xiaodie, and it took four months to build. It has created a world of glass. Being in it is like being in a mirror palace, crystal clear and dazzling. The construction cost reached 30,000 yuan. On September 18th at 2:00 PM, the opening ceremony will be held simultaneously with the four major distribution centers of the China Asia-Pacific Electrical Appliance Factory, the Zhanghua Woolen Textile Factory, and the China Ceramics Company. The business will officially start on September 19th, selling September 18th commemorative goods. Each set, originally priced as high as two or three yuan, will be sold for 9.18 yuan to commemorate the national humiliation with a spirit of struggle, not a gesture of decline and sorrow.

Investigation of Fake Military Officer Case Not Completed 181

Yin Bohong, from Shandong, and Dong Shujin, from Anhui, who lived at 21 Rue Conty, recently privately established the Fifth Route Headquarters of the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army in room 39 of the Huadong Apartments on Avenue du Roi Albert, issuing appointment letters indiscriminately and defrauding people of money for their own use. Procedures for Obtaining Saltpeter and Sulfur Passports 185

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to various industry associations yesterday, stating that it had received instructions from the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, which stated that it had received an order from the Ministry of Industry stating that it had received a consultation from the Ministry of Finance. Since the administration of saltpeter and sulfur affairs in various provinces was transferred to the Ministry, the Ministry had already consulted with the Ministry of Military Affairs and submitted it to the Executive Yuan for approval. In the future, industrial and commercial enterprises applying for special transport passports for saltpeter and sulfur should report the required quantities according to the category of essential goods to the local salt affairs agencies. After verifying the purpose, they should submit it to the Ministry, which would then consult with the Ministry of Military Affairs for approval, and issue a circular to instruct compliance. The Ministry's internal and external transport documents are now issued directly by the provincial authorities in charge of saltpeter and sulfur. Those that have established saltpeter and sulfur bureaus, such as Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, Anhui, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Shandong, Fujian, Hebei, and Henan, have already been taken over and jointly managed by the local salt affairs agencies. Those that have not established saltpeter and sulfur bureaus, such as Sichuan, Guizhou, Yunnan, Guangdong, Guangxi, Shaanxi, Qinghai, Gansu, Suiyuan, Rehe, Chahar, and Xinjiang, should submit applications for passports and transport documents to the highest salt affairs agency in their respective provinces for verification and issuance. The saltpeter and sulfur affairs of Guizhou are temporarily handled by the Sichuan Transport Commissioner, and the saltpeter and sulfur affairs of Sichuan are handled by the Sichuan Transport Commissioner and the North Sichuan Transport Deputy Commissioner, according to the salt distribution area. Shaanxi is temporarily handled by the Hedong Transport Commissioner, Shanxi is temporarily handled by the North Jin Revenue and Transport Bureau, and Chahar is temporarily handled by the North Mongolian Salt Bureau. Suiyuan is handled separately by the North Jin Revenue and Transport Bureau and the Koubei Mongolian Salt Bureau according to the salt distribution area. The Ministry should consult with the Ministry for verification, etc. With this approval, the Bureau should be informed and instructed to inform, etc. In response, a letter is hereby sent, hoping for verification, etc.

Cruel Mother-in-Law Abuses Daughter-in-Law; Neighbors Outraged 189

Representatives were elected to go to the police station to request an investigation

Wang Ni, a Ningbo woman, is 43 years old. Because her husband died many years ago, she was unaccustomed to being alone and became acquainted with Zhong Xiaoxiang, a fellow villager, and lived with him at 63 Risheng Lane, Dongjiadu, Nanshi. Wang Ni had a son from her previous marriage, named Zhixi, who is 23 years old and works as a worker in a foundry. He also lives with his mother and Zhong. In the first month of last year, Wang Ni, through a matchmaker, hired Lu Jinhui, the daughter of Lu Xiaohu, as her daughter-in-law (now 18 years old). After she married into the family, the relationship between the couple was not very harmonious, and Wang Ni was inherently mean, with her neighbors calling her a shrew. When treating Jinhui, she was initially kind, but when Jinhui slightly offended her, she was whipped. Zhixi, her son, and Zhong Xiaoxiang, her lover, also listened to Wang Ni and helped her to abuse Jinhui. As a result, Jinhui was covered in wounds and suffered greatly. Yesterday morning, after Wang Ni got up, Jinhui got a basin of water and asked her mother-in-law to wash her face. However, because her voice was slightly low, Wang Ni did not hear her. When Wang Ni caught sight of the washbasin on the table, she accused Jinhui of not greeting her and immediately slapped the woman twice on the cheek. Jinhui knew that Wang Ni's bad temper was raging and there was no reasoning with her, so she could only secretly shed tears and sob quietly. Wang Ni was still not satisfied and used the leather shoes that her lover was wearing to beat Jinhui all over her body. Where the shoes hit, the skin broke and bled. However, Jinhui did not dare to cry out or resist. It was not until Wang Ni was exhausted that she stopped and said sternly to Jinhui, "Be careful tonight." In the evening, after Zhong Xiaoxiang and Wang Zhixi returned home for dinner, Jinhui took off her coat and was about to go to bed when Wang Ni and Zhixi unexpectedly entered the room. They first stuffed cotton into Jinhui's mouth to prevent her from making a sound, then grabbed her hands and feet and beat her severely. In this bad environment, Jinhui had no choice but to moan. However, this faint sound reached outside and was heard by Rong Weng, who lived in the same residence. Knowing that Wang Ni was displaying her power again, he tiptoed to the door of Jinhui's bedroom. Seeing that the door was tightly closed, he peeked through the crack and saw this tragic scene. He was furious and immediately returned to his room, opened the window, and loudly gathered the neighbors. They kindly advised Wang Ni and the others not to abuse their daughter-in-law like this. Unexpectedly, Wang Ni and the others cursed at the neighbors. The neighbors could not bear it any longer and discussed it that night. At 3:00 PM yesterday afternoon, Fang Aiqing, Sha Heshang, Chen Jinzhi, Xu Hongfu, Li Aqing, Xue Asan, Liu Fusheng, Zhang Quanyou, Zou Xiaoxing, and a dozen other residents of the neighborhood represented all the residents and went to the first police station in the district to report the situation and request an investigation. Chief Yi immediately sent the police to the neighborhood and arrested Wang Ni. However, her son Wang Zhixi and the others were not at home, so they were not arrested. Wang Ni, along with her daughter-in-law Jinhui, were taken back to the station. After a preliminary hearing, it was found that Jinhui was indeed covered in wounds and blood stains. It was deemed that Wang Ni's abuse of her daughter-in-law was inhumane. Wang Ni was temporarily detained and the police were ordered to arrest Wang Zhixi and the others and send them to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Jingcheng Silk Weaving Factory Negligent, Causing Fire 190

Yuan Shiquan Detained for Kidnapping a Girl 191

Yu Mingzhang, from Chongming, lives in Chongzheng Bridge in Suzhou City. He has a daughter named Yu Xiulin, who is nine years old this year. Yu Xiulin is lovely and cute. Because Yu Mingzhang works as a cook outside, and his wife does needlework, their daughter is left unattended at home. The kidnapper Yuan Shiquan, who is from the same village, used picture cards and food as bait to lure her out. However, his cousin Sun Buting works at the Xiaoshadu Construction Factory in Shanghai, so he immediately sent a letter to instruct him to pay attention to the search. It was not until the day before yesterday that Sun found out and reported to Yu Mingzhang, who came to Shanghai to look for her. He found her there and immediately called the police to arrest Yuan Shiquan and send him to the Fifth District Second Precinct, who transferred him to the District Court for trial.

First Meeting of the National Games Competition Committee 212

Discussion of Ball Games Competition Rules and Other Issues

Walking and Marathon as Performance Events

(Nanjing, 15th) The National Games Competition Committee held its first meeting at the Ministry of Education on the 15th, chaired by Shen Liang. It was decided: (1) Whether the women's basketball court should be 60 feet long, with a two-zone system, six players per team, and a center circle jump. If there is a tie, should it be handled according to the rules of men's secondary schools? It was decided that the preliminary round will be divided into four quarters, each lasting seven minutes. If there is a tie, it will be extended twice, each time lasting two minutes. The semi-finals and finals will have a time of eight minutes per quarter. If there is a tie, it will be extended twice, each time lasting two minutes. (2) When serving in volleyball, according to the volleyball rules, players must not jump with both feet, and at least one foot must be on the ground, and must not cross the line. (3) The list of referees was approved. (4) What kind of tennis balls should be used for the National Games tennis competition? Please contact Shen Siliang in Shanghai. (5) The existing baseball field does not meet the regulations. Can baseball be changed to be held on the football field, and softball be held on the baseball field? Please Zhang, the general secretary, make a temporary decision and temporary competition venue rules. (6) The national martial arts competition will follow the regulations, with seven championship events, and each event will not be divided into other championship events. (7) The issue of adopting the marathon race will be based on performance, with a minimum of 40 people. Accommodation and meals will be at their own expense, and train tickets will be handled in the same way as ordinary athletes. (8) The national martial arts performance will be divided into four categories, with a limit of six people per category. (5) Committee member Chu's proposal that the ten dos and don'ts for athletes be passed. (10) Accommodation for referees from October 8th to 22nd, in 60 rooms in the Central Hotel, with three people per room. (10)(1) Shen Siliang, Chu Minyi, Qin Chonghou, Ma Yuehan, Wu Bangwei, and Huang Ming were appointed as members of the sports equipment review committee, with Shen as the chairman. (10)(2) Create a temporary badge for the organizing committee. (10)(3) It was decided to hold another meeting on the afternoon of October 9th. The National Games has entrusted the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the China Travel Service to forward reduced-price boat and train tickets for overseas Chinese and local groups to Guangdong's Tan Guohua, who will come to Beijing to negotiate the food, accommodation, and transportation issues for the athletes. Donations for prizes will be requested from various agencies and accounted for by the conference as a whole.

Page 20

Most Perfect Low-Frequency Amplification 238

Li Yuanqing

The low-frequency amplification commonly used in radios today can be roughly divided into three types:

(1) Resistance-Coupled Amplification: This type of amplification occupies a small space, is low in cost, and also because it uses non-inductive resistors, its value remains constant at any frequency, so the sound quality obtained is the clearest. However, it itself has no amplification effect. If you want to get a large volume, you must increase the number of amplification stages, which is its disadvantage.

(2) Transformer-Coupled Amplification: Transformer-coupled amplification is now the most widely used low-frequency amplification. It can obtain a very large amplification factor with a small amount of power. However, the magnetic inductance of the low-frequency transformer is inversely proportional to the direct current passing through it. If the current is large, the magnetic inductance will be reduced. If the current exceeds the specified value, the transformer core will be saturated, which will have a great impact on the sound quality.

(3) Push-Pull Amplification: To obtain a large and undistorted sound, push-pull amplification must be used. However, push-pull amplification consumes a lot of power, and it is not often used in small-scale radios.

In addition, there is also a type called choke coil amplification, which is similar in form and function to resistance amplification. Very few radios use this type of amplification method now, so it is omitted.

Low-frequency amplification occupies a very important position in the radio. Carelessness in design can affect the efficiency of the entire machine. Therefore, it is necessary to be extra cautious before installation.

The low-frequency amplification introduced in this article is designed using the principle of filtering. It combines resistance coupling and transformer coupling (originally named Resistance-fed Transformer Coupling), so that it grasps the advantages of both sides, while minimizing the disadvantages of both sides.

As shown in the figure, R is a 500,000 ohm resistor, C is a ol mtd capacitor, and T is a commonly used low-frequency transformer. (B + is changed to B -) When used, the plate direct current only passes through R. The primary coil of the transformer only passes through the fluctuating low-frequency current. Since there is no direct current passing through the transformer, its magnetic inductance can remain unchanged, and the danger of saturation can also be avoided. Therefore, the sound wave obtained is not only very clear, but also larger in volume than that of using transformer coupling alone.

We know that the primary coil of the transformer is most easily burned out, but if the above method is adopted, then there is no direct current passing through the coil, so this kind of loss can of course be reduced. It is also necessary to mention this feature incidentally.

Adjustment Method and Steps for Shortwave Transmitters (Continued) Luo Jingyu 239

Below: Steps to Adjust a Feedback Oscillator Transmitter

In order to stabilize the frequency, large-power, long-distance communication stations often use feedback oscillator transmitters. For example, the current international radio stations in Shanghai, such as Fenglin Bridge, all use this type.

As mentioned earlier, a feedback oscillator transmitter uses a small vacuum tube to generate oscillation, and then amplifies it through several stages before sending it to the antenna. Therefore, the feedback oscillator first avoids changes in the plate capacitance due to the high heat of the vacuum tube plate power, and second, it avoids the influence of the antenna part directly coupled to the oscillation circuit. However, in today's most popular feedback oscillator, the oscillation is not generated by the method of returning the plate current to the grid, but by using a crystal to generate a qualitative oscillation, as shown in Figure 4. When the frequency of LC itself resonates with the crystal quartz, there will be a considerable amount of electricity to the grid circuit, causing the quartz to oscillate. Once the quartz oscillates, even if the frequency of LC changes, it will not affect the oscillation frequency of the quartz. The magnitude of its frequency is purely determined by its thickness. The shorter and thinner it is, the higher its frequency will be. However, it is very difficult to find a method with appropriate thickness for ordinary shortwave applications. Therefore, there is an application for a frequency multiplier. For example, if we want to transmit 20 meters, if the oscillation frequency of the quartz is 1875 kHz (160 meters), then after the first frequency multiplier, it becomes 3750 kHz (80 meters), and after the second to third, it becomes 15000 kHz (20 meters). Therefore, the structure of today's new transmitters mostly has the following procedure:

In the figure, the first stage is a quartz-controlled oscillator with a frequency of F. The second stage is called a buffer amplifier, which further expands the original F to make it more stable. Then the third, fourth, and fifth stages are all frequency multipliers, which multiply the frequency to 8F. The sixth and seventh stages are to forcefully amplify the 8F after the fifth multiplication (Power Ampl) ify) and send it to the antenna for outward transmission. (To be continued)

What's Inside a Vacuum Tube? Zijing 240

The term "vacuum tube" is already very common. As the name suggests, we know that a vacuum tube is a glass tube with nothing inside. But vacuum tubes are not really vacuum. The facts tell us that there are indeed many things inside this tube that we cannot imagine.

Suppose there is now a round glass ball with a diameter of 5 o'clock, and the air inside has been pumped out to a considerable degree by a vacuum pump. In other words, it can be said to be a vacuum. However, there are still the following things inside this glass tube:

(1) Nitrogen molecules: 288,300,000,000,000

(2) Gas molecules: 77,600,000,000,000

(3) molecules: 3,450,000,000,000

(4) Carbon dioxide molecules: 644,000,000,000

(5) Radon molecules: 4,470,000,000

(6) molecules: 25,000,000

(7) molecules: 5,000,000

Moreover, although there are 369,998,495,000,000 molecules moving around in this tube, it does not feel crowded. As for the air pressure inside the ball, it is only one millionth of the atmospheric pressure. If the air pressure inside the ball is equal to the atmospheric pressure, then there will be 28,988,423,520,000,000,000 molecules present. Therefore, until now, there is no absolute vacuum tube in this world.

Trivia (Continued) Number of Electricity 241

(5) Manufacturing Moisture-Proof Wood: Wood has a small density and easily absorbs moisture. If you are making the outer casing of a radio, it is often the case that the radio reception is poor due to the air being too humid. It is best to first apply the following chemicals evenly to the wood panel: Method A: Saturated solution of zinc chloride,

Method B: Six parts boric acid, five parts ammonium chloride, three parts borax, add 100 parts water,

Choose either of the above two methods. After it is completely dry, apply paint to prevent moisture absorption.

(6) Polishing Discarded Records: Cut the discarded record (i.e. phonograph record), first use coarse sand to smooth out the fine lines, then use fine sandpaper to rub it, and then use a cloth dipped in sesame oil to rub it in one direction until it is polished. Hard rubber or plastic boards can also be polished in this way, but avoid the step of removing the lines with coarse sandpaper.

(7) Lubricant: Soap applied to the saw blade can prevent it from being astringent when sawing wood. Applied to screws, it is easy to screw into the wood and also easy to disassemble. (8) Cleaning Files: When filing hardware or wood plastic boards with a file, the filings will gather on the file teeth. Because of this reason, the file is easily dulled. It is best to apply chalk powder to the file teeth before use. After use, immerse it in a dilute acidic liquid for half an hour (if the debris gathered on the teeth is wood or plastic board debris, use dilute sulfuric acid; if it is hardware debris, use dilute hydrochloric acid). After taking it out, rinse it with clean water once, then wash it with salt water many times. After drying, rub it with an oiled cloth. This not only does not damage the file teeth, but also makes it faster and faster. (End)

Small Experiences 242

Simple Method for Connecting Wires - Steelyard

Inside a radio, the circuit is crisscrossed, and the number of wires accounts for almost two-thirds of the entire machine, and their function is also extremely important. Once it is broken even a little bit, the radio reception will be cut off immediately. Therefore, the method of connecting wires is extremely important. Coarser wires can be soldered, but the wires inside the speaker, headphones, and transformers are often above number 40, then the procedure is difficult to implement. With the following method, as long as your hands are quick and your eyes are sharp, the work will be very reliable. First, disassemble the original parts that have been inspected and are considered to have broken wires, find the broken ends, and prepare for work. Put the two ends of the break at the same time in the lower outer flame of the flame (the type of flame is related to the number of the wire, see below). Wait for them to melt into small balls, immediately make the two ends contact in the flame, and they will be connected in one place, and immediately take them out of the flame.

After the joint has cooled, apply paint or resin to the exposed copper to prevent current leakage, and then it can be used. The flame used is a gas stove for number 28 to number 30, an alcohol lamp for number 30 to number 40, and a candle flame for numbers above 40.

If you are familiar with this method, you can make the interface as thick as a solder, and the conductivity is also very good.

New Barometer - Celebration 243

When receiving broadcasts on the radio on a clear day, it is usually very quiet. Suddenly, a continuous crackling of static is heard, and it becomes louder and louder. This is a sign that it will rain or thunder. Conversely, when receiving broadcasts on a rainy day, if the static gradually decreases, this is a sign that the weather will clear up.

Investigation 245

— Baihe

Missionaries from Western countries are not afraid of the barbarity and uncivilized nature of savage peoples. They cross oceans and come to China, and then distribute themselves to the interior of China to conduct systematic investigations, clearly and thoroughly investigating the transportation, situation, production, customs, education, and military preparations of all provinces, towns, and cities in China. Many places are not as familiar to Chinese people as they are to foreign missionaries. Take the map of China as an example. It is still necessary to go to bookstores in Britain, the United States, or Japan to buy a (China Map) to recognize the edition, which may be more reliable than the (actual survey) by the Chinese themselves. It is shameful to say that this is only a small aspect. To (talk about it), it is really (unspeakable).

However, when Chinese people go abroad, it is very different. What they hear and see and report to our people is either how prosperous the clothing and food life in New York is, or how mysterious the glass dance halls in Paris are. Or how gentle the Japanese geisha are, and how lewd the French prostitutes are.

Some time ago, the Japanese organized (Manchuria and Mongolia Inspection Groups) and (Manchuria and Mongolia Investigation Teams) to engage in investigation work in the eastern and western provinces. Many reports have already been seen in this process. Details are not spared about mountains, rivers, forests, minerals, agricultural products, animal husbandry, customs, household registration, geology, economy, education, and climate. However, what we used to read in the travel notes of Chinese travelers was only that a certain kind of strange fish was produced in a certain place in the Northeast, and the taste was quite delicious; a certain kind of exotic bird was produced in a certain place, which could be used for making ornaments. In some places, the marriage customs were prevalent with polygamy; in some places, both men and women liked to have wild sex. In some places, wives were exchanged for cattle and sheep; in some places, they could even spend the night in the homes of strangers and have sex with their wives and daughters.

However, Chinese travelers who investigate these strange customs are still considered to have some significance. In the metropolis, there are countless foreign talents and well-dressed high-ranking Chinese people who specialize in investigating which school beauty, which queen, opened a warehouse somewhere last night, which concubine, which star, has a relationship with someone in this process, which is really meaningless.

A Farmer's Words 246

— Qingqu

The day before yesterday, there was a farmer in his old age. He brewed a pot of tea under the Fahua Pagoda in the early morning. He said to himself, "This time a (flower collector) has come, it's really terrible!" (In the local dialect of Jiading, a hurricane is called a flower collector, because the cotton is blown off by the wind, so it has this name.) After saying that, he sighed a few times, full of resentment. After a while, he continued loudly, "We farmers always rely on the sky for food. Unfortunately, God is not willing to take care of us. Even if we put in capital and work hard, alas! As long as there is a strong wind and heavy rain, then the snow-white cotton field, every flower is copper money (according to the farmer's tone), will turn into nothing. On weekdays, we look forward to catching two full loads of good flowers. (Picking flowers in the field is called catching flowers.) Who knows that it is just empty happiness. Alas! It is directly said that heaven raises people, but heaven is not willing to raise people, and people cannot ask heaven for help." After saying that, he continued to sob!

When I heard this, I couldn't help but feel moved. I asked him, "Which village do you come from?" He said, "I come from Dongxiang. How is the wind disaster in Dongxiang this time?" "Alas! Don't mention it. This year's cotton, at first glance, seemed to be a year of great harvest. Unexpectedly, it was blown by the wind for a day and a night, and then by a burst of heavy rain, which caused the cotton boll on the stalk to fall off. (The two words Ludo are from a foreign language, that is, Hualing, which is still used in our city.) Originally, each plant had at least a dozen or more, up to thirty or more, which can be said to be unseen in thirty years. Now, when I look at the field, most of them have fallen on the soil. If it hadn't been for the disaster, they could have been caught in the hand. Even if there are a few left, they are still weak and turn into yellow flowers, and they will not be able to sell for money in the future. This is a huge loss, more than the disaster in the 20th year of the Republic of China!"

After hearing this, I thought it was worth asking him more clearly, so I asked him, "Which village's cotton is the best this year?" He said, "The best is Dongnan and Erxiang, Beixiang is second, and Xixiang is second again. Dongxiang had already caught sixty or seventy catties by the end of last month. On average, it was always around thirty or forty catties. If the weather is not out of balance, there is hope for a good harvest. Jiading farming has always been (cotton seventy percent, rice thirty percent). Assuming about 600,000 acres are cultivated, and then discounted to 400,000 acres of cotton fields, this time the disaster is estimated to be a lot? Each cotton plant only needs four flower bolls, and one acre can harvest two loads of flowers. If there is no wind and rain this year, not to mention other things (this year's products from the fields are all harvested), some flowers are also eaten firmly. (The farmer's tone, those who eat firmly, means stable.)" I also asked him, "Is the rice not damaged by the cotton like this?" He said, "The rice is still good because it was planted later. It is now (doing belly) (doing belly, that is, when the nutrients in the stem are flourishing), and it has not yet bloomed. If there is a strong wind and heavy rain later, this is (rice is only afraid of the wind), then it is really bad luck!" After hearing this, I felt that the old man was really speaking from experience, so I drank a loud voice, pulled him away, and at the same time, the applause and laughter of the audience were regarded as a farewell.

Five steps, the first thing that was reflected in my eyes was the four large hollow characters (Open-air Stage) written in chalk, and the handwriting was very strong. This was much larger than what I saw in three steps. There were seven or eight people singing and drumming together, and there were also many self-made crowns, robes, and beards, but the actors in the theater were painting colors on their faces, but they were covering themselves with soot.

Six steps, a group of colorful girls are enjoying the cool, waiting for the people who have not returned. No, not all of them, they are sellers of flesh, waiting for their employers. In several places, they are even forcibly implementing their pulling and pushing methods.

Seven steps, when a person who looked like an upper class man got out of the rickshaw, because the rickshaw puller said a sentence, he simply slapped him twice. The copper coins that should have been given were scattered on the ground. The rickshaw puller bent over, holding his face with one hand and picking up the coins with the other.

Eight steps, a group of shabby and dirty children are scrambling for cold rice and leftovers in a worker's rice bucket and vegetable bowl.

Nine steps, just as a beggar came from behind, stretching out his hand and shouting, "Young master, do a good deed."

Ten steps, a young man wearing a tattered military uniform was constantly shaking a diamond ring in his hand in front of people's eyes. Two men, one wearing a long gown and one wearing a short suit, came to his side.

Four Company Commanders of the Northeast 247

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Fifteen The guest leaves with shy tenderness and a smile, and the old bad news arrives, bringing sorrow and anxiety.

He kept making the sound of leather shoes all the way to the gate, feeling that he was a bit neurotic. There was only a little acquaintance between them. Could it be said that this was love that came at the sound of his approach? Men talk about love, always like this. Thinking like this, he stepped out of the gate with one foot, but he heard a very unnatural subtle cough behind him. Looking back, it turned out to be Guizhi standing at the foot of the wall outside the gate. When he turned back to look at her, she also smiled and lowered her head. Zhao Ziqiang's heart was active, and he expected that she must have been standing here meaningfully, so he stood still and nodded to her. Guizhi looked back at the gate, and then took a step closer, and asked Zhao Ziqiang in a low voice: "Did you tell the old man about what happened in the milk tea shop just now?" Zhao Ziqiang paused and smiled: "No, I didn't tell him about it." Guizhi said: "Did you really not say it?" Zhao Ziqiang said sternly: "We still have things to say in the future. If we say it now, it would be bad, wouldn't it?" Guizhi blushed and said: "I didn't mean it that way. Because my family is still very old-fashioned, if it were like Miss Huang, my family would not agree." Zhao Ziqiang had nothing to say, and nodded repeatedly, saying "yes" several times. Guizhi smiled and said: "I have nothing to say, please go." Zhao Ziqiang saw that she did not avoid entering the gate, but asked herself to leave, so of course she did not want to turn her back to people. This feeling was deepened. The smile in his heart was inexplicably surging up on his face, and he also whispered: "Tomorrow, tomorrow, still at that milk tea shop, do you think it's okay?" Guizhi pondered for a while before smiling and asking: "Do you have anything to say?" Zhao Ziqiang stood and thought for a while before smiling and saying: "I don't have anything to say, but I want to follow Xiaotian's words and come back to Haidian every time. It would be best if we could talk and exchange opinions at the milk tea shop." Guizhi didn't say anything, just smiled at him. (188)

Within Ten Steps 248

— Sleeping Buddha

These are the ten different impressions I got from the first step to the tenth step after leaving the entrance of XX Lane.

One step, a group of people were surrounding a very small wooden table. There were two pieces of red and black glued to the two ends of the table. A young man sitting in the center was only using his left hand to move a circular bamboo tool in his palm. When the person showed the bamboo tool, the people who were helping out followed and shouted for a while. Then, there was the tinkling sound of silver coins. However, this was just an approximation. The one who watched the most carefully was a woman standing in front of the table. She kept digging in her pocket, and the beads of sweat on her forehead had no more room to hang on. The clear and round sweat that was squeezed down from time to time was like broken pearls.

Two steps, a young man in student attire, but already very dirty, was squatting on the cement and constantly writing, writing. There were already quite a few people watching, and there were three or five copper coins scattered sparsely on the cement. Three steps, a hunchbacked middle-aged man was playing the erhu, and a little girl of twelve or thirteen was standing beside him singing. Four steps, the patrol was next to a passerby, confiscating an opium pipe. They stood talking for a while. Suddenly, they stopped an old man who looked like a countryman and a young man in military uniform and bargained. At the same time, a middle-aged man came from the left and raised the folded photo in his hand and asked in a low voice: (Do you want erotic pictures?)

Confucius once said: (Within ten steps, there must be fragrant grass.) This kind of luck is of course enviable. However, if Confucius were to live in modern times, he would definitely not dare to say such definite words again. Especially in Shanghai, the fragrant grass within ten steps has long become Guangling San.

The Evolution of Men 272

—旅隼

It may be a bit blasphemous to say that the mating of animals is love. However, animals also have sexual lives, and that cannot be denied. When their spring emotions are aroused, the females and males are together, inevitably having a bit of "you and I" time. Of course, the females sometimes pretend to be aloof, running a few steps and looking back, even making a few calls, until they carry out "cohabitation love." Although there are many kinds of animals and their "love" methods are complex, there is no doubt about one thing: the males do not necessarily have any privileges.

Humans are the most intelligent of all creatures, and the first thing is that men are very capable. In the beginning, it was rough and sloppy, but because of the saying "knowing the mother but not knowing the father," the women once "ruled" for a period of time. At that time, the old grandmothers were probably more powerful than the later clan chiefs. Later, I don't know how, women became unlucky: their necks, hands, and feet were all locked with chains,扣 with rings, and 环 although these rings have mostly become gold and silver over the millennia, and are镶 with pearls and real diamonds, these necklaces, bracelets, rings, etc. are still symbols of female slaves. Since women have become slaves, then men don't have to ask her for her consent to love) her. In ancient tribal wars, the result was that the captives would become slaves, and the female captives would be raped. At that time, the spring emotional arousal period had probably been "cancelled," and the male master could rape the female captives and female slaves anytime and anywhere. Modern gangsters and villains do not treat women as human beings, but in fact, it is a great legacy of chieftain-style chivalry.

However, although the ability to rape is already a step in the "evolution" of humans compared to animals, it is only semi-civilized after all. Think about it, how much fun can there be in a woman crying and wringing her hands? Since the appearance of money, this treasure, men's evolution has really been amazing. Everything in the world can be bought and sold, and sexual desire is naturally no exception. Men can spend a few stinky coins to get what they want from women's bodies. And he can say to her: I am not raping you, you are willing, you are willing to take these coins, you have to do this and that, do whatever I say, we are doing a fair transaction! After trampling on her, he also wants her to say "Thank you, Young Master." Is this something that animals can do? Therefore, prostitution is a fairly high stage of human evolution.

At the same time, the old-fashioned marriage of parents' orders and matchmakers' words is even more brilliant than prostitution. Under this system, men get permanent, lifelong living property. When the bride is put on the groom's bed, she only has obligations, she doesn't even have the freedom to protect the price, let alone love. Whether you love it or not, in the name of the Duke of Zhou and Confucius, you have to be faithful to the end, you have to maintain your chastity. Men can use her at any time, but she has to abide by the etiquette of the sages. Even if (evil thoughts are only moved in the heart, it is considered to have committed adultery. If male dogs use such clever and severe methods on female dogs, the female dogs will definitely be anxious to (jump over the wall). However, people will only jump into wells and become virtuous women, chaste women, and heroic women. The evolutionary significance of etiquette marriage can also be imagined.

As for men being able to use (the most scientific) theories to make women, even without etiquette, be willing to be single-minded to the end, and deeply believe that sexual desire is a (beastly desire) and should not be used as the basic condition for love; therefore, inventing (scientific chastity), that is, of course, the pinnacle of civilized evolution.

Alas, people Men are different from animals!

Self-Note: This article is a defense of morality

Stomach Disease 273

— 何如

Stomach disease is really a terrible disease, especially linked to men of letters. Everyone knows that Su Manshu died of stomach disease, although he was a monk, he liked to eat braised beef with wine, and did not keep the Buddhist precepts, so he deserved to die, but because he was a wandering man of letters whose nationality and family background were not clear, it aroused the sympathy of several men of letters. Then there was Luo Heizhi, who also died of stomach disease, but he also suffered from heart disease, so when he walked, he either frowned and held his heart, or held his stomach with a bitter face. I remember it was early spring in 1928, when a friend who had just come to Nanjing from Changsha told me that Luo Heizhi was dead I was stunned by this unfortunate news, and I couldn't speak for a long time. I wrote a short poem mourning him:

Stealing a living in the world is also hard,

Burning the fire of the heart to turn the wheel of the heart.

Manshu did not make Jin Si die,

Spring grass is born in Jiangnan again.

Later, I heard that Heizhi's death, although originally ill, was because he was imprisoned for an article, and he was so angry that he died a few days after being released from prison, so I wrote another short poem mourning him

I wish to write a hundred thousand words of articles,

Dig out the liver and shed blood to tell the troubles.

The moon is like a lamp and the flower is like a pen,

Long stand by the soul of poetry to comfort the nine springs.

Two months ago, I saw Peng Jiahuang for the first time in front of Le Sibing's sickbed. He said that appendicitis was very dangerous, and Mr. Le was considered safe, but he himself often suffered from stomach problems. I saw that his haggard face, with a deep melancholy look, was a bit like Heizhi But I never expected that he would die soon. Naturally, it is not uncommon for Hunan people to suffer from stomach diseases, because they have no chili, and chili that is so spicy that they shed tears cannot be eaten with rice. Ten years ago, I suffered a very serious stomach disease. I lay in Xiangya Hospital and adopted a food reduction therapy. I starved for almost a month before I was considered to be starved. Since then, I have not dared to eat chili. For the past two or three years, I felt that the stomach disease had not occurred for nearly ten years. Seeing that the friends from my hometown were all spicy, and every time I ate with them, my throat was itchy and strangely hard to endure, so I tried the spicy taste. At the same time, because of the hardship of life, I often bought drunk to forget my worries, so my stomach disease broke out again. Now that I see Peng Jiahuang's death, I remember the distress of Heizhi's illness, and I also think of Zhu Jianfan's incurable stomach cancer. Is stomach disease so terrible

Correcting Mr. Qian Gechuan's Distortions 274

— Suo Yuan

Mr. Qian said: (If we all had literary talent, we could, like Japan's Akita Ujaku, change course and learn Esperanto.) This is not true. Although classic works by Shakespeare, Pushkin, Gogol, Goethe, etc., have been translated into Esperanto, and recently, works such as "All Quiet on the Western Front" and "Roar, China!" have also been translated into Esperanto, the application of Esperanto is not limited to "literature." Sun Yat-sen's "Three Principles of the People" has been published in Esperanto, and "The Collected Works of Lenin" in Esperanto is also being compiled and translated. Because its "grammar is extremely simple and changes are regular," it is free from the "trouble of removing facial hair" and the inability to produce a menu. Therefore, "no literary talent is needed," and anyone can learn it. Those who have learned a certain foreign language will naturally find it easier to learn Esperanto, and it will definitely not be harmful to the foreign language already learned, so there is no such thing as "changing course."

Mr. Qian cited an example to prove that Esperanto does not work in "mainland China" hospitals, resulting in being given "several injections of saline." This is truly "deliberate hypothetical evidence to confuse the public." Taking a step back, even if Mr. Qian's hypothetical citation is possible, I think it would also be difficult for patients and nurses everywhere to converse using Basic English. If a patient needs "several injections of saline," they cannot use the word "syringe" but must say "a type of pointed tube with a plunger that uses air pressure to release water from its skin and then releases it into a very fine line for gardening, treatment, etc." (See "International Daily Selection," No. 40, "A Critique of Basic English by the British"). It can be seen that one still cannot avoid "looking angry."

Mr. Qian said that Esperanto's "shortcomings are that it is too early, its uses are uncertain, and even mixing written and spoken language is considered too lacking in books for us to read." Yes, Esperanto has only been around for forty-six years, and compared with the literature of various national languages, it is inferior in "quantity." However, just in terms of learning books, there are over ten million copies compiled in fifty-two languages (see E. Drezen's "The Problem of International Language," 1932 edition, pages 2-3). According to the International Radio Commission statistics, in 1929, various countries gave 2,006 speeches and reports in Esperanto. Esperanto is an international language, so it cannot be estimated solely by the "quantity" of its use. But what about Basic English? It was published in 1930, so its "duration" is knowable. Besides ten small booklets, what else is there? Is there a restaurant in the world that knows how to cook "(the white root that makes your eyes water)" or "(the bird that Noah sent out to see if there was land, cooked on the stove)" (roast pigeon)? Can its "uses" be said to be broad?

Mr. Qian said: (Because Russian is too difficult and cannot force people to learn it well, Russia uses Esperanto to communicate with the proletariat of various countries.) This is a distortion of Esperanto. It is not worth the laughter of knowledgeable people. The popularity of Esperanto in Russia is because they recognize the necessity of an international language and the practicality of Esperanto. Esperanto itself is just a language, and it is certainly not impossible for it to be a tool for the proletariat of various countries, but it can also be used for other purposes. Let's take the facts in China as an example: In 1921, the Seventh National Education Conference of China held in Guangzhou resolved to add Esperanto to the curriculum of normal schools. The Nanjing Central Party Headquarters also compiled and printed "The Shandong Question," "The May 3rd Jinan Incident," and "The Tanaka Memorial" in Esperanto. As for the literature of various small and weak nations being transplanted to China, it was not through English or Basic English, but mostly through Esperanto, as evidenced by the translations of Esperanto comrades Zhou Zuoren, Hu Yuzhi, Wang Luyan, Ba Jin, Sun Yong, and Zhong Xianmin.

The above is a correction to Mr. Qian's misinterpretations. There is still much to say about Mr. Qian's claims, but I cannot allow "Free Talk" to be exclusively for my and Mr. Qian's "battleground," and the inaugural issue of Guanghua Bookstore's "Reader Monthly" ("Special Issue on Critique of Basic English") will also be published soon. If I discuss with Mr. Qian again, it should also be published in "Reader" or other places. Now I summarize my main points of view on Basic English: (1) No national (country's) language should be an international language; (2) Basic English violates language development, is anti-evolutionary, and is something that goes backward; (3) Basic English, due to its circuitous expression, is not easier than English, and is even worse than Esperanto; (4) Basic English is not a reasonable, appropriate, and usable plan for making English more logical.

### Six Dynasties Love Songs with the Same Motif 275

— Zhao Jingshen

We know that folk literature is oral literature, passed down from person to person and from generation to generation. Therefore, regardless of the place, whether it is China or foreign countries, or the time, whether it is ancient or modern, we often find the same ballads or stories. The Six Dynasties love songs collected in the "Yuefu Poetry Collection" are no exception. Now, I list the similarities as follows:

(1) I think of my beloved, you travel with an unrestrained heart. Mist and dew hide the lotus, seeing the lotus is unclear.

(Note) This is one of the "Zi Ye Songs" and also appears in "Du Qu Ge," except that the first line is: (My heart is always uneasy,) "(Zi)" is made "(Huan,)" and "(Bu)" is made "(Ju.)"

(2) Relying on love as if to advance, shy and unwilling to come forward. Vermilion lips sing enchanting songs, jade fingers play delicate strings.

(Note) This is one of the "Zi Ye Songs" and also appears in "Zi Ye Jing Ge," except that "(Kou Zhu)" is made "(Zhu Kou.)"

(3) Looking up at the paulownia tree, the paulownia flowers are especially pitiful. I wish heaven had no frost or snow, so the wutong seeds could last for a thousand years.

(Note) This is one of the "Zi Ye Four Seasons Songs" and also appears in "Du Qu Ge," except that the first line is missing.

(4) The yellow swan flies into the sky, hesitating halfway. A chariot wheel turns in its belly, do you know who it is thinking of?

(Note) The previous three were merely transformations of Wu-style songs, that is, transformations within the Wu region. This is the "Huang Hu Song" of the Wu region and also appears in the "Xi Qu Ge Xiangyang Yue" of the Jingxiang area, except that the last line is: (Who does Huan pity today?)

(5) Long mast, iron deer's tail, cloth sail rises gracefully. Woe is me, where am I going, three thousand miles away.

(Note) This is the "Ao Nong Ge" of the Wu-style songs and also appears in the "Wu Ye Ti" of the "Xi Qu Ge," except that "(San)" is made "(Shu.)" (6) Sobbing and weeping in the dark, the setting sun shines into the tent. What is the suffering without oil, just let it be light tomorrow.

(Note) This is one of the "Du Qu Ge." There is also another song with the same title, the first two lines of which are (Lower the curtain, the lights are out, the bright moon shines into my bosom.) Also, "(Shi)" is made "(Ling.)" Perhaps these two songs are connected, just like the repeated chapters of the Book of Songs and the repeated sections of Yuan opera, and it is not necessarily a transformation. What is strange is that these two songs are not placed together but are separated by as many as thirty-three songs.

(7) Tonight we have happily parted, when will we meet again? The bright lamp shines on the empty chessboard, the date is distant and uncertain.

(Note) This is one of the "Zi Ye Songs" and also appears in "Du Qu Ge," (Tonight we have) is made (Holding hands with.)

(8) The apes of the Three Gorges of Badong cry sadly, crying three times at night, tears stain the clothes. (Note) This is the "Daughter's Son" of the "Xi Qu Ge" and also appears in the "Wu Xia" of "Miscellaneous Ballads and Songs." The "(Ye)" ape is made "(Yuan)".

Shallow Lake (6) 276

— By Joseph Conrad, translated by Shi Heng

(Time passes quickly… rumors arose among the women… our enemies were on the alert… my brother became gloomy, I began to think of killing and cruel death… Our race, like yours, the white race, must obtain what it loves. There is a time when men will forget loyalty and respect for elders. Power or prestige is given to a leader, but love, strength, and courage are given to all men. My brother said to me: (You can snatch her from among them. The two of us are like one person.) So I replied: (Do it quickly, because I feel that without her by my side, even the sun has no warmth.) Our opportunity came, and the chief took all the people with torches to the mouth of the river to fish. Thousands of small boats were released, and on the white sand between the water and the forest, leaf huts were built for the chief's family. Smoke rose like a blue mist of the night, and the voices of countless people cheerfully echoed in the area. As they were preparing their boats to go fishing, my brother came over and said to me: (Tonight!) I inspected my weapons, and when the time came, our boat joined the circle of countless boats lit by torches. The firelight flashed on the water, but behind the boats was darkness. When the shouting began and people were clamoring like madmen, we escaped. The water swallowed our torches, and we drifted back to shore, where it was dark except for the faint glow of occasional embers. We could hear the conversations of the slave women between the huts. Then we found a quiet and desolate place. We waited there. She came. She ran along the coast, quickly and without leaving a trace, like a leaf about to be blown into the sea by the wind. My brother said gloomily: (Go and carry her onto our boat.)

I held her in my arms. She was panting, her heart beating against my chest. I said:—I have taken you from those people. You ran to me in response to the call of my heart, but my arms must resist the will of the great one to carry you into my boat! (It is right,) my brother said: (We are a people who must obtain our desires, and we can withstand the majority of people. We should have snatched her in the daytime.) Then I said: (Let's set off;) because since she had come onto our boat, I began to think of the many people under the chief's command. (Yes, let's go,) my brother said: (We have been cast out from the group. Now this small boat is our country, and this sea is our hiding place.) One of his feet was still lingering on the shore, and I urged him to hurry up, because I remembered her heart beating against my chest, and I also thought that two people could not withstand a hundred people. We set off, going down the riverbank; when we passed the bay where they were fishing, the shouting had stopped, but the murmuring of the people was as noisy as the buzzing of insects at noon. Many boats drifted together in clusters, in the red glow of the torches, in the misty haze: people talked about games, those people, arrogant, boasting, mocking, who in the morning might still have been our friends, but by night had become our enemies. We rushed past quickly. We no longer have friends in our homeland. She sat in the middle of the boat, covering her face; as silent as she is now; as invisible as she is now, I do not regret my departure, because I can hear her breathing beside me—just as I can hear it now.)
